        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer1239235545">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer5833610887871742871">3.5-4 (I keep going back and forth) <br /><br />I liked this book, a lot, and part of the reason I can't fully enjoy it is because my shitty Amazon copy came without any of the photos it should have had. <br /><br />But the other part for me was that there was limited character interaction and a long time between animals, so it felt like a lot of feeder material while we waited for the good stuff. <br /><br />His tales of airport woe and corrupt officials while at times humorous also left me wanting more than just a peek inside th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText5833610887871742871">3.5-4 (I keep going back and forth) <br /><br />I liked this book, a lot, and part of the reason I can't fully enjoy it is because my shitty Amazon copy came without any of the photos it should have had. <br /><br />But the other part for me was that there was limited character interaction and a long time between animals, so it felt like a lot of feeder material while we waited for the good stuff. <br /><br />His tales of airport woe and corrupt officials while at times humorous also left me wanting more than just a peek inside their airport, maybe if he was going to have such limited animal time we could have had more of an overall overview of the places he was traveling. <br /><br />The parts with the animals were really heart breaking, the world is in a sad state. Googling about some of these animals now (being that this book took place in 1988) it was sad and interesting to see where those animals stand now.. For instance, the white rhino is worse off than it was 27 years ago when conservation started, while the sweet kakapo looks like it may stand a chance of surviving despite our attempts to snuff it out. <br /><br />All in all- a good solid read. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="5833610887871742871">...more</a>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_929936873">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/929936873" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/27248823-vishal" class="left imgcol" title="Vishal"><img src="http://d.gr-assets.com/users/1418477422p2/27248823.jpg" alt="Vishal" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/929936873?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jul 02, 2015</a>

      <a href="/user/show/27248823-vishal" class="user" title="Vishal">Vishal</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer929936873">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer2592199328730337287">What happens when you go on a virtual trip with Douglas Adams to distant islands and dense rainforests, looking for the rare wildlife that are on the brink of extinction and we only have the Last Chance to See them?<br /><br />You are entertained, you are informed, you learn and at the end you are blown away with the message this book drops on you. You become a sadder and a wiser person by the time you finish this, and it'll make you want to convey a message to fellow human beings: <strong>read this book, please.</strong><br /><br />Th</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText2592199328730337287">What happens when you go on a virtual trip with Douglas Adams to distant islands and dense rainforests, looking for the rare wildlife that are on the brink of extinction and we only have the Last Chance to See them?<br /><br />You are entertained, you are informed, you learn and at the end you are blown away with the message this book drops on you. You become a sadder and a wiser person by the time you finish this, and it'll make you want to convey a message to fellow human beings: <strong>read this book, please.</strong><br /><br />The author travels to many countries and islands, most of which are third world countries like Indonesia, Zaire and others; where the bureaucracy is engrossed in deeply rooted corruption and persistent lack of any effective action in animal conservation projects. He describes the difficulties he faced in travelling, staying at hotels and getting the essential stuff of requirements at those places. First, it might seem that he's whining about the problems he had to face, but later you realise that he's making a point to the reader that how difficult it is for the naturalists and activists to get there and start working in such circumstances with sheer reluctance of any local authorities to provide any help. Needless to say, Northern White Rhinoceros from African forests have gone extinct now and the numbers of the Komodo dragon from one of the Indonesian islands remains unchanged after more than two decades of publishing this book.<br /><br />While some islands like New Zealand and Mauritius, have better awareness among the administration and general public. This has helped a lot and the birds which were on the critical stage of extinction, are now saved. China, too can be said to be among the better informed nations with better resources, but sadly, the Chinese are more interested in eating any thing that moves and it makes them hungrier still for 'special' food if they could find a species on extinction stage. This is what has happened with Yangtze dolphin in Yangtze river of China, where the dolphins are eaten to extinction. These incidents make it very, very clear that how necessary it is for everyone to get an idea about our environment, our flora and fauna what our fellow humans have done to them. For us humans to thrive on this planet, we need a stable ecosystem with all the animals thriving with their natural rate of survival/extinction, because that's what makes a stable ecosystem and the world a likely place to live in.<br /><br />Coming back to the book, it has been written in a very clear and lucid manner and if you have read any science fiction by Adams, then I may as well tell you that this is so different from anything Adams has ever written. The text is simple, funny and moving; and if you happen to be one of those people who couldn't digest the absurdities of his fiction, this is the book for you. Realistic and gives you the pleasure of an almost effortless reading.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="2592199328730337287">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/206092107?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Sep 15, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/1392605-maggie" class="user" title="Maggie">Maggie</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>



        


          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a href="/review/list/1392605-maggie?shelf=book-club" class="actionLinkLite">book-club</a>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer206092107">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4297851818530363746">Of the two travel journals of comedic writers I've read recently (the other being <a title="The Innocents Abroad or, The New Pilgrims' Progress (Modern Library Classics) by Mark Twain" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2443.The_Innocents_Abroad_or__The_New_Pilgrims__Progress__Modern_Library_Classics_">The Innocents Abroad: or, The New Pilgrims' Progress</a>), this one was more fun and more substantive. Douglas Adams wrote with sadness and hope about the plight of animals who are charmingly ill-suited to the world that has changed around them. <br /><br />In a more serious work than the books I know him for, he expresses his awe and empathy and discomfort along the way with a lot of clarity -- enough for me to empathize with him</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4297851818530363746">Of the two travel journals of comedic writers I've read recently (the other being <a title="The Innocents Abroad or, The New Pilgrims' Progress (Modern Library Classics) by Mark Twain" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/2443.The_Innocents_Abroad_or__The_New_Pilgrims__Progress__Modern_Library_Classics_">The Innocents Abroad: or, The New Pilgrims' Progress</a>), this one was more fun and more substantive. Douglas Adams wrote with sadness and hope about the plight of animals who are charmingly ill-suited to the world that has changed around them. <br /><br />In a more serious work than the books I know him for, he expresses his awe and empathy and discomfort along the way with a lot of clarity -- enough for me to empathize with him and get a sense of what it really was like, for him, to come into contact with the animals, and with the conservationists who are a breed of their own. <br /><br />This book taught me a lot about some rare animals and tactics for saving them. It made me remember some of the concern I had as a child hearing about endangered species, which had gone out of my consciousness for a while. And it made me laugh, too. </span>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/623094903?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">May 23, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/20644400-niki-k" class="user" title="Niki K.">Niki K.</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer623094903">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16528175191456641487"> Last Chance to See is a book documenting the journeys of Douglas Adams and Mark Carwardine as they explore the corners of the Earth in search of endangered species. Adams, a comedic author, and Carwardine, an expert zoologist, travel everywhere from the jungles of Madagascar to the Yangtze River in hopes of encountering species on the verge of extinction. Adams and Carwardine shed some light on these rare species in hopes of promoting awareness and influencing recovery efforts. This book greatl</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16528175191456641487"> Last Chance to See is a book documenting the journeys of Douglas Adams and Mark Carwardine as they explore the corners of the Earth in search of endangered species. Adams, a comedic author, and Carwardine, an expert zoologist, travel everywhere from the jungles of Madagascar to the Yangtze River in hopes of encountering species on the verge of extinction. Adams and Carwardine shed some light on these rare species in hopes of promoting awareness and influencing recovery efforts. This book greatly stresses the importance of rescuing these unique animals.<br /><br />	Last Chance to See is an incredibly informative and descriptive book. It doesn’t overlook a single detail and allows the reader to easily envision these unusual animals and their surrounding environments. Not only does it clearly describe the appearance of these animals, but a large portion of this book covers why these species have reached a point of near extinction and the current environmental issues they face. <br /><br /> After reading this book, it has made me rethink how valuable our Earth and its animals are. It’s made me be more concerned with these animals and influences me to do anything in my power to keep animals from reaching near extinction. Because humans are the main reason for extinction and endangerment, it also makes the reader feel bad. However, it’s very inspiring and makes the reader stress more importance on wildlife. <br /></span>

<span id="freeTextContainer10266580035696922321"><em>"I didn't notice that I was being set upon by a pickpocket, which I am glad of, because I like to work only with professionals. Everybody else in the shop did notice, however, and the man was hurriedly manhandled away and ejected into the street while I was still busy choosing buns. The baker tried to tell me what had happened, but my Zaïrois French wasn't up to it, and I thought he was merely recommending the curranty ones, of which I therefore bought six."</em><br /><br />Douglas Adams wrote this series of ess</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText10266580035696922321"><em>"I didn't notice that I was being set upon by a pickpocket, which I am glad of, because I like to work only with professionals. Everybody else in the shop did notice, however, and the man was hurriedly manhandled away and ejected into the street while I was still busy choosing buns. The baker tried to tell me what had happened, but my Zaïrois French wasn't up to it, and I thought he was merely recommending the curranty ones, of which I therefore bought six."</em><br /><br />Douglas Adams wrote this series of essays as he traveled with zoologist Mark Carwardine to try to get a glimpse of animals on the verge of extinction. There's wonderful humor to it as they navigate these exotic locations and unfamiliar cultures, but he also manages to capture the seriousness of the situations for these creatures and for the balance of life on this planet if extinction rates continue to accelerate.<br /><br />As much as I loved the <em>Hitchhiker's Guide</em> books back in the day, I think this might be my favorite Douglas Adams book. It had been at least ten years since I last read it, but it held up amazingly well. I'm reminded once again that Adams left us far too soon.<br /><br /><img class="escapedImg" src="http://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/photo.goodreads.com/hostedimages/1380375306r/729847._SX540_SY540_.jpg" /></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer620010442">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16329644068384176260"><strong>Last Chance to See: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://readwithstyle.wordpress.com/2013/11/14/last-chance-to-see-douglas-adams-and-mark-carwardine/" target="_blank">http://readwithstyle.wordpress.com/20...</a></strong><br /><br />The name of Douglas Adams is of course very well-known to me, mainly because of his eternal comic science fiction series The Hitchhiker’s Guide to the Galaxy, which I must shamefully admit I still haven’t read. Anyway, I had already heard of Adams’s sarcastic sense of humour, but I didn’t at all expect to see it in a book about animals. Because that is exactly what Last Chance to See is. The science fiction author collaborated with the</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16329644068384176260"><strong>Last Chance to See: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://readwithstyle.wordpress.com/2013/11/14/last-chance-to-see-douglas-adams-and-mark-carwardine/" target="_blank">http://readwithstyle.wordpress.com/20...</a></strong><br /><br />The name of Douglas Adams is of course very well-known to me, mainly because of his eternal comic science fiction series The Hitchhiker’s Guide to the Galaxy, which I must shamefully admit I still haven’t read. Anyway, I had already heard of Adams’s sarcastic sense of humour, but I didn’t at all expect to see it in a book about animals. Because that is exactly what Last Chance to See is. The science fiction author collaborated with the zoologist Mark Carwardine on an ambitious project around the world to see, probably for the last time, some of the species on the brink of extinction. Last Chance to See was simultaneously turned into a BBC radio documentary series and later into a TV series of the same name.<br /><br />It all started quite innocently (if you can actually describe a trip to Madagascar as something innocent). Adams and Carwardine travelled to the island to see the aye-aye, a lemur and one of our closest relatives.<br /><br />From this journey the idea to travel the world in search of nearly extinct species arose. For a couple of years Carwardine organized the trip, while Adams was finishing yet another of his books. According to the zoologist, they used a big map of the world. Adams pinned where he wanted to go and Carwardine in turn pinned the places with the endangered animals. The result is one of the most fascinating journeys into the world wildlife.<br /><br />Read more: <a rel="nofollow" href="http://readwithstyle.wordpress.com/2013/11/14/last-chance-to-see-douglas-adams-and-mark-carwardine/" target="_blank">http://readwithstyle.wordpress.com/20...</a></span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16329644068384176260">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6PCZKorEz/MfPtrzoqZKFjisdZ+EMbMmT3jG6gnhL2qNJKb5eBbbCZPmrkjcx6ykcVu2hs3s9IwlccN4xXTZLw==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

Twenty years later, comic genius Stephen Fry is returning with Mark to see if the species still exist. A major BBC television series follows the two on six separate journeys which take them to the Amazon basin, East Africa, Madagascar, New Zealand, Indonesia and Mexico to look for a flightless parrot, the Amazonian manatee, man-eating Komodo dragons, man\'s closest living relative, the northern white rhino and an animal so bizarre it seems to have been assembled from bits of other creatures. These are not just travels to the four corners of the world, but a journey in time to open our eyes to what humans have done to the Earth in the 20 years since the original Last Chance to See expeditions. Adams made the universe a much funnier place to inhabit and forever changed the way we think about towels, extraterrestrial poetry, and especially the number 42. And then, too soon, he was gone.Just who was this impossibly tall Englishman who wedded science fiction and absurdist humor to create the multimillion-selling five-book “trilogy” that became a cult phenomenon read round the world? Even if you’ve dined in the Restaurant at the End of the Universe, you’ve been exposed to only a portion of the offbeat, endearing, and irresistible Adams mystique. Have you met the only official unofficial member of Monty Python’s Flying Circus? The very first person to purchase a Macintosh computer? The first (and thus far only) author to play a guitar solo onstage with Pink Floyd? Adams was also the writer so notorious for missing deadlines that he had to be held captive in a hotel room under the watchful eye of his editor; the creator of the epic computer game Starship Titanic; and a globetrotting wildlife crusader.A longtime friend of the author, Nick Webb reveals many quirks and contradictions: Adams as the high-tech-gadget junkie and lavish gift giver . . .irrepressible ham and painfully timid soul . . . gregarious conversationalist and brooding depressive . . . brilliant intellect and prickly egotist. Into the brief span of forty-nine years, Douglas Adams exuberantly crammed more lives than the most resilient cat–while still finding time and energy to pursue whatever side projects captivated his ever-inquisitive mind. By turns touching, tongue-in-cheek, and not at all timid about telling the warts-and-all truth, Wish You Were Here is summation as celebration– a look back at a life well worth the vicarious reliving, and studded with anecdote, droll comic incident, and heartfelt insight as its subject’s own unforgettable tales of cosmic wanderlust. For the countless fans of Douglas Adams and his unique and winsome world, here is a wonderful postcard: to be read, reread, and treasured for the memories it bears.From the Hardcover It\'s also a book full of entertainment and wonders.  In The Song of the Dodo, we follow Quammen\'s keen intellect through the ideas, theories, and experiments of prominent naturalists of the last two centuries. We trail after him as he travels the world, tracking the subject of island biogeography, which encompasses nothing less than the study of the origin and extinction of all species. Why is this island idea so important? Because islands are where species most commonly go extinct -- and because, as Quammen points out, we live in an age when all of Earth\'s landscapes are being chopped into island-like fragments by human activity.  Through his eyes, we glimpse the nature of evolution and extinction, and in so doing come to understand the monumental diversity of our planet, and the importance of preserving its wild landscapes, animals, and plants. We also meet some fascinating human characters. By the book\'s end we are wiser, and more deeply concerned, but Quammen leaves us with a message of excitement and hope.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"6769878573058426212\" href=\"#\" Unlike their human counterparts, who must alter their environment to accommodate our physical limitations, animals are adaptable to an amazing range of conditions--i.e., radical changes in a creature\'s physiology take place to match the demands of the environment.     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/4.Douglas_Adams">About Douglas Adams</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
      <a href="/author/show/4.Douglas_Adams"><img alt="4" src="http://d.gr-assets.com/authors/1189120061p2/4.jpg" class="right" /></a>
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer7574866493988255718">Douglas Noël Adams was an English author, comic radio dramatist, and musician. He is best known as the author of the <a title="Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11.Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy">Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</a> series. Hitchhiker's began on radio, and developed into a "trilogy" of five books (which sold more than fifteen million copies during his lifetime) as well as a television series, a comic book series, a computer game, and a feature film that was comp</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText7574866493988255718">Douglas Noël Adams was an English author, comic radio dramatist, and musician. He is best known as the author of the <a title="Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/11.Hitchhiker_s_Guide_to_the_Galaxy">Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</a> series. Hitchhiker's began on radio, and developed into a "trilogy" of five books (which sold more than fifteen million copies during his lifetime) as well as a television series, a comic book series, a computer game, and a feature film that was completed after Adams' death. The series has also been adapted for live theatre using various scripts; the earliest such productions used material newly written by Adams. He was known to some fans as Bop Ad (after his illegible signature), or by his initials "DNA".<br /><br />In addition to <em>The Hitchhiker's Guide to the Galaxy</em>, Douglas Adams wrote or co-wrote three stories of the science fiction television series Doctor Who and served as Script Editor during the seventeenth season. His other written works include the Dirk Gently novels, and he co-wrote two Liff books and Last Chance to See, itself based on a radio series. Adams also originated the idea for the computer game Starship Titanic, which was produced by a company that Adams co-founded, and adapted into a novel by Terry Jones. A posthumous collection of essays and other material, including an incomplete novel, was published as <a title="The Salmon of Doubt" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/359.The_Salmon_of_Doubt">The Salmon of Doubt</a> in 2002.<br /><br />His fans and friends also knew Adams as an environmental activist and a lover of fast cars, cameras, the Macintosh computer, and other "techno gizmos". <br /><br />Toward the end of his life he was a sought-after lecturer on topics including technology and the environment.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="7574866493988255718">...more</a>

    </div>
    <a href="/author/show/4.Douglas_Adams" class="actionLink moreLink">More about Douglas Adams...</a>
